## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of population change (dP/dt) as a function of time and current population size, which is a classic population dynamics problem. The relationship likely involves density-dependent growth models where growth rate depends on current population level.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Exponential (Malthusian) growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Unlimited resources, population grows proportionally to current size'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate decreases logarithmically as population approaches carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with flexible curvature near carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Population has a minimum viable size below which it declines'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy-type growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Growth as balance between anabolic (power-law) and catabolic (linear) processes'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth'}
- {'name': 'Power-law density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Growth rate as a power of population size'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous analog', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Per-capita reproduction saturates with density, linear mortality'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent exponential growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate changes exponentially over time (e.g., changing environment)'}
- {'name': 'Logistic with time-varying rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * exp(c2 * t)', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth in a temporally changing environment'}
- {'name': 'Quadratic density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3', 'scenario': 'Polynomial expansion of density-dependent growth'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent decline → Negative quadratic term in P: growth ~ c0*P - c1*P**2 indicates logistic-type saturation
- Allee effect / bistability → Cubic polynomial in P with sign changes indicates multiple equilibria and minimum viable population
- Logarithmic saturation → log(c/P) or log(P) terms indicate Gompertz-type slowly decelerating growth near capacity
- Metabolic scaling in growth → Fractional power laws P**c with 0 < c < 1 reflect allometric/metabolic constraints on growth
- Separable vs non-separable time dependence → If dP/dt depends on t beyond through P, the environment is non-stationary; multiplicative time factors exp(c*t) or polynomial t terms indicate external forcing
- Ratio of production to loss → dP/dt as difference of two terms (gain - loss) with different P-dependence indicates competing biological processes
- Per-capita rate analysis → dP_dt / P being a decreasing function of P signals negative density dependence and self-regulation
- Inflection point asymmetry → Power or theta parameters in logistic-like models control whether maximum growth rate occurs below or above half carrying capacity

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.201(-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233)P + 0.201P + \frac{0.201P}{1 + \exp(-5.637(-0.634 + P))}$$

Let me simplify the first term. Let me denote $c = 0.201$, $a = 5.637$, $b = 10.233$.

First term: $c(-1 + P/a)(1 - P/b)P$

Expanding: $c \cdot P \cdot (-1 + P/a)(1 - P/b) = c \cdot P \cdot [-1 + P/b + P/a - P^2/(ab)]$
$= c \cdot P \cdot [-1 + P(1/a + 1/b) - P^2/(ab)]$
$= c[-P + P^2(1/a + 1/b) - P^3/(ab)]$

So the GT has the form:
$$f(P) = -cP^3/(ab) + cP^2(1/a+1/b) - cP + cP + \frac{cP}{1 + e^{-a(-0.634+P)}}$$

The $-cP + cP$ cancels! So:

$$f(P) = -cP^3/(ab) + cP^2(1/a+1/b) + \frac{cP}{1 + e^{-a(P - 0.634)}}$$

This simplifies to:
$$f(P) = \alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{1 + e^{-\delta(P - \epsilon)}}$$

where $\alpha = -c/(ab) \approx -0.00348$, $\beta = c(1/a + 1/b) \approx 0.0553$, $\gamma = c \approx 0.201$, $\delta = a \approx 5.637$, $\epsilon \approx 0.634$.

The GT has three essential components:
1. A cubic term in P ($P^3$)
2. A quadratic term in P ($P^2$)
3. A **sigmoid-weighted** term: $\frac{P}{1 + e^{-\delta(P-\epsilon)}}$

The sigmoid term $\frac{P}{1+e^{-\delta(P-\epsilon)}}$ is a fundamentally non-polynomial, non-exponential, non-logarithmic function. It's specifically a logistic-sigmoid times P.

Note: $\frac{P}{1+e^{-\delta(P-\epsilon)}}$ can also be written using $\log(\exp(\cdot)+1)$ since $\frac{d}{dx}\log(e^x+1) = \frac{1}{1+e^{-x}}$, but the integral relationship doesn't help directly.

However, $\frac{cP}{1+e^{-a(P-p_0)}}$ is NOT equivalent to $c\log(e^{aP}+1)$ or simple exponentials.

Let me now check each candidate systematically.

### Candidates with `t` dependence
The GT has no `t` dependence. Candidates with `t` can only match if all `t`-dependent terms can be zeroed out.

**Candidate 8**: Has $c5 \cdot \exp(P \cdot c6) \cdot \sin(c6 \cdot t + c7)$ - can set $c5=0$ to eliminate. Remaining: $P(Pc0+c1) + c2\exp(P^2 c3)$. This is quadratic + Gaussian-like in P. No sigmoid term. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 18**: $P(Pc0+c1) + c2\sin(c3t+c4) + c5\exp(Pc6) + c7$. Set $c2=0$. Remaining: $P^2c0 + Pc1 + c5e^{Pc6} + c7$. Has polynomial + exponential but no sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 19**: $P(c0(Pc1+1)e^{c2t} + c3(P+c4)(Pc5+1))$. Set $c0=0$: $Pc3(P+c4)(Pc5+1)$. This is a polynomial (cubic). No sigmoid. But GT has sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 20**: Set $c2=0$: $Pc0(Pc1+1) + Pc3 + P^{c4}c5$. Polynomial + power law. No sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 21**: Set $c2=0$: $P(c0(Pc1+1) + c3((Pc4)^{c5}-1))$. Power law, no sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 24**: Has $\exp(c2t)$ and $\exp(c5t)$. Setting both to zero kills everything. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 25**: Set $c5=0$: $Pc0(Pc1+1) + Pc2 + P^{c3}c4$. Polynomial + power law. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 26**: Set $c5=0$: polynomial. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 27**: Set $c3=0$: $P^3c0 + Pc1(Pc2+1)$. Cubic polynomial. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 28**: $\frac{c0t+c1 + (P(Pc2+c3)+c4e^{Pc5})(c6t+c7)}{c6t+c7}$. Set $c0=0$: $\frac{c1}{c6t+c7} + P(Pc2+c3) + c4e^{Pc5}$. Still has $t$ dependence unless $c1=0$. Then: $P^2c2 + Pc3 + c4e^{Pc5}$. Polynomial + exponential, no sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 60**: Set $c3=0$ (in sin): $P(Pc0+c1) + c2 + c3\exp(0) = P(Pc0+c1) + c2 + c3$. Wait, let me re-read. $c3\exp(Pc4\sin(c5t+c6))$. Set $c3=0$: $P(Pc0+c1)+c2$. Quadratic. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 62**: Similar to 28 but with $\exp(P^2c5)$. Set $c0=0, c1=0$: $P(Pc2+c3)+c4\exp(P^2c5)$. No sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 63**: Set $c2=0$: $P(Pc0+c1)+c5\exp(P^2c3)+c7$. No sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 69**: $Pc0(Pc1+1) + c2\sin(c3t+c4) + c5\log(c6e^{Pc7}+1)$. Set $c2=0$: $Pc0(Pc1+1) + c5\log(c6e^{Pc7}+1)$. 

Now, $\log(c6 e^{Pc7}+1)$. If $c6 = e^{-c7 \cdot p_0}$ for some $p_0$, then $\log(e^{c7(P-p_0)}+1)$. This is a softplus function. But the GT has $\frac{cP}{1+e^{-\delta(P-\epsilon)}}$, which is P times a sigmoid, NOT a softplus. These are fundamentally different functions. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 72**: Set $c5=0$: $Pc0(Pc1+1) + P^{c2}c3\log(Pc4+1)$. No sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 73**: Has $\exp(c2t)$ and $\exp(c4t)$. Set both to zero: everything vanishes. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 74**: Rational in $t$. For this to be $t$-independent, need specific conditions. $\frac{P^2c0t+P^2c1+Pc2t+Pc3+c4t+c5}{c6+t}$. For $t$-independence: $\frac{(P^2c0+Pc2+c4)t + P^2c1+Pc3+c5}{t+c6}$. This is $t$-independent iff $P^2c0+Pc2+c4 = k(t+c6)/t$... No, for it to be constant in $t$: $(P^2c0+Pc2+c4) = \lambda$ and $P^2c1+Pc3+c5 = \lambda c6$. But $P^2c0+Pc2+c4$ depends on P, so $\lambda$ depends on P. Then $f = P^2c0+Pc2+c4$. This is quadratic. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 77**: Has $Pt$. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 78**: Has $c3t$. Set $c3=0$: $(P^3c0+P^2c1+Pc2+c4)/(P+c5)$. Rational function. **[NO MATCH]** (same as candidate 80 analysis below)

**Candidate 79**: Set $c0=0$: $(P+c3)^2(Pc4(Pc1+c2)+Pc5+c6)/((P+c3)^2(Pc1+c2)) = (Pc4(Pc1+c2)+Pc5+c6)/(Pc1+c2) = Pc4 + (Pc5+c6)/(Pc1+c2)$. This is rational. No sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 81**: Set $c4=0$: $P(Pc0+c1)+c2\exp(P^2c3)$. No sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 82**: Set $c1=0, c4=0$ (to kill $e^{c2t}$ terms): $P(Pc0+c3)+c5$. Quadratic. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 83**: Set $c2=0$ (in exp): $c4=1$, so $Pc2(Pc3+1) = Pc2 Pc3 + Pc2$. Wait, re-read: $P^2c0+Pc1+Pc2(Pc3+1)\exp(c4t)+c5$. Set $c2=0$: $P^2c0+Pc1+c5$. Quadratic. **[NO MATCH]**

### Pure polynomial candidates
The GT has a sigmoid component which is NOT polynomial. So pure polynomials cannot match.

**Candidate 58**: $Pc0(P+c1)(Pc2+1) = c0c2P^3+c0P^2+c0c1c2P^2+c0c1P = c0c2P^3+(c0+c0c1c2)P^2+c0c1P$. Cubic polynomial. **[NO MATCH]**

### Rational function candidates (polynomial/polynomial)

The GT has a sigmoid term. A rational function of polynomials cannot produce a sigmoid. Let me verify this claim: $\frac{P}{1+e^{-a(P-p_0)}}$ is NOT a rational function of P.

**Candidate 1**: $(P^4c0+P^3c1+P^2c2+Pc3+c4)/(P+c5)$. Rational. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 2**: $P(P^3c0+P^2c1+Pc2+c3)/(P+c4)$. Rational. **[NO MATCH]**

$= c0/(Pc1+c2) + P(Pc3+c4) + c5\exp(Pc6)$
$= P^2c3 + Pc4 + c5e^{Pc6} + c0/(Pc1+c2)$

This has polynomial + exponential + rational terms. No sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

Wait, there's a naming collision with c2 and c3 appearing in multiple places. Let me just note this has $\exp(P^2 c5)$, which is a Gaussian-type term, not a sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

### Candidates with exp(P*c) (single exponential in P)

GT = $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{1+e^{-\delta(P-\epsilon)}}$. 
The exponential $e^{Pc4}$ is NOT the same as $\frac{P}{1+e^{-\delta(P-\epsilon)}}$. **[NO MATCH]**

### Candidates with log terms

$\log(c4 e^{Pc5}+1)$: softplus-like. GT needs P*sigmoid. Different. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 46**: $P(Pc0+Pc1\log(Pc2+1)+c3)$. Has $P^2\log(P)$ type terms. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 47**: $P(Pc0+c1+c2\log(c3(P+c4)+1))$. Has $P\log(P)$ type terms. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 48**: $P(Pc0+c1+c2\log(Pc3+1))$. Has $P\log(P)$ type terms. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 61**: $P^2c0+Pc1+c2+c3\log(P^2c4+1)$. Has $\log(P^2)$ type terms. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 70**: $P^2c0+Pc1+c2\log(c3\exp(Pc4)+1)$. Softplus. Not P*sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 71**: $P(Pc0+c1)+c2\log(c3\exp(Pc4)+1)$. Same as 70 essentially. **[NO MATCH]**

Wait, let me reconsider candidates 70 and 71 more carefully. The GT sigmoid term is $\frac{cP}{1+e^{-a(P-p_0)}}$. Can this be expressed using softplus?

$\frac{P}{1+e^{-x}} = P \cdot \sigma(x)$ where $x = a(P-p_0)$.

Softplus: $\log(1+e^x) = \int \sigma(x) dx$ (with respect to x).

$P \cdot \sigma(a(P-p_0))$ vs $\log(1+e^{a(P-p_0)})$. These are fundamentally different - one is P times sigmoid, the other is softplus. They cannot be made equal by any constant choice. **[NO MATCH]** confirmed for 70, 71.

### Candidate 5
$P(Pc0+c1)+c2\exp(Pc3)+c4\log(c5\exp(Pc6)+1)$

This has: quadratic in P + exponential + softplus.

The GT has: cubic in P (specifically $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2$) + P*sigmoid.

Can $c2\exp(Pc3) + c4\log(c5 e^{Pc6}+1)$ equal $\alpha P^3 + c4' \frac{P}{1+e^{-\delta(P-\epsilon)}}$ minus the quadratic part?

No. $\exp(Pc3)$ is an exponential, and $\log(c5 e^{Pc6}+1)$ is softplus. Neither produces a cubic term or P*sigmoid. **[NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 6

### Candidate 15

$= Pc0 + (Pc3+c7)/(Pc1+c2) + c4\exp(Pc5)\log(Pc6+1)$

$= Pc0 + (Pc3+c6)/(Pc1+c2) + c4\log(Pc5+1)$

### Candidate 75
$P(P^2c0+(P+c1)(Pc2+c3+c4\log((P+c5(P+c6))/P)))/(P+c1)$

This has log terms. The argument of log simplifies: $(P+c5P+c5c6)/P = 1+c5+c5c6/P$. So $\log(1+c5+c5c6/P)$. This is a log(rational) type term. **[NO MATCH]**

Let me reconsider whether I might be missing something. The GT has a sigmoid term $\frac{P}{1+e^{-a(P-p_0)}}$. Which candidates could potentially produce this?

The sigmoid $\frac{1}{1+e^{-x}}$ can be written as $\frac{e^x}{1+e^x}$. So $\frac{P}{1+e^{-a(P-p_0)}} = \frac{Pe^{a(P-p_0)}}{1+e^{a(P-p_0)}}$.

None of the candidates have a structure that produces $\frac{P}{1+\exp(\cdot)}$ or equivalent. The closest are softplus candidates (log(exp+1)) and pure exponential candidates.

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider whether the GT could be well-approximated by simpler functions over a restricted domain. But the rules say NO approximations - exact equivalence only.

Let me double-check candidate 5 one more time:
$P(Pc0+c1) + c2\exp(Pc3) + c4\log(c5\exp(Pc6)+1)$

Note that $\frac{d}{dP}[\log(c5 e^{Pc6}+1)] = \frac{c5 c6 e^{Pc6}}{c5 e^{Pc6}+1} = \frac{c6}{1+c5^{-1}e^{-Pc6}}$

So the derivative of softplus gives a sigmoid, but softplus itself is not P*sigmoid. These are different.

I'm now confident that none of the candidates can exactly match the GT.

Wait, actually let me reconsider more carefully. The GT after simplification is:

$$f(P) = \alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{1 + e^{-\delta(P - \epsilon)}}$$

Could any candidate reproduce this? The key challenge is the $\frac{P}{1+e^{-\delta(P-\epsilon)}}$ term.

Note: $\frac{P}{1+e^{-x}} = P - \frac{P}{1+e^x}$. Also $\frac{P}{1+e^{-x}} = P \cdot \sigma(x)$ where $\sigma$ is the logistic sigmoid.

None of the candidates have an explicit sigmoid or $P/(1+\exp(\cdot))$ structure.

Could a combination of exp and log produce this? $\frac{P}{1+e^{-x}} = P \cdot e^x/(1+e^x)$. If we had $P \cdot e^x - P \cdot \log(1+e^x) \cdot e^x/(1+e^x) \cdot ...$, no, this doesn't simplify.

Actually, I realize I should look at this differently. Let me re-examine the original GT before simplification:

$$f(P) = c_0(-c_1 + P/c_2)(c_3 - P/c_4)P + c_5 P + \frac{c_6 P}{c_7 + \exp(-c_8(-c_9 + P))}$$

With the given constants, $c_0 = c_5 = c_6 = 0.201$, $c_1 = c_3 = 1$, $c_7 = 1$, $c_2 = c_8 = 5.637$, $c_4 = 10.233$, $c_9 = 0.634$.

The first two terms give: $0.201(-1+P/5.637)(1-P/10.233)P + 0.201P$

Expanding: $0.201P[(-1+P/5.637)(1-P/10.233) + 1]$
$= 0.201P[-1+P/10.233+P/5.637-P^2/57.68 + 1]$
$= 0.201P[P/10.233+P/5.637-P^2/57.68]$
$= 0.201P^2(1/10.233+1/5.637) - 0.201P^3/57.68$
$= 0.201P^2 \cdot 0.2752 - 0.00348P^3$
$= 0.0553P^2 - 0.00348P^3$

So indeed: $f(P) = -0.00348P^3 + 0.0553P^2 + \frac{0.201P}{1+e^{-5.637(P-0.634)}}$

This confirms my analysis. The function requires a P*sigmoid term that none of the candidates can produce.

Actually, hold on. Let me reconsider whether any candidate could match if we think about it differently. What if the sigmoid term can be absorbed into a different functional form over the non-negative domain?

$\frac{P}{1+e^{-a(P-p_0)}}$ for $P \geq 0$: at $P=0$, this equals 0. As $P \to \infty$, it approaches $P$. It's a smooth, monotonically increasing function. It's NOT equivalent to any polynomial, rational function, exponential, log, sin, or power law function.

I'm confident: **none of the candidates match**.

Let me do one final check on candidates that have the most complex structures:

**Candidate 15**: $Pc0 + \frac{Pc3+c7}{Pc1+c2} + c4 e^{Pc5}\log(Pc6+1)$. The $e^P \log(P)$ term is a different basis function. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 75**: Has $\log((P + c5(P+c6))/P) = \log(1+c5+c5c6/P)$. For large P this approaches $\log(1+c5)$, a constant. Not sigmoid-like. **[NO MATCH]**
